## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |

| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# LLVM IR Type System to Code Generation Chain

## Your Task

Trace how LLVM IR types flow from the type creation API to code generation in llvm/llvm-project. Find C++ source files implementing: the Type class hierarchy (IntegerType, FunctionType, StructType), the type system's context ownership, and the IR type to machine type lowering in SelectionDAG.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/llvm-project--a8f3c97d, sg-evals/gcc--96dfb333.

## Summary

I traced the LLVM IR type system from type creation to code generation in `github.com/sg-evals/llvm-project--a8f3c97d`. Here's the complete chain:

### 1. Type Class Hierarchy
- **`llvm/include/llvm/IR/Type.h`** — Base `Type` class with `TypeID` enum (IntegerTyID, FunctionTyID, StructTyID, etc.)
- **`llvm/include/llvm/IR/DerivedTypes.h`** — Derived type classes: `IntegerType`, `FunctionType`, `StructType`, `ArrayType`, `VectorType` (Fixed/Scalable), `PointerType`, `TargetExtType`
- **`llvm/lib/IR/Type.cpp`** — Implementations of all factory methods (`IntegerType::get`, `FunctionType::get`, `StructType::get`, `StructType::create`, `PointerType::get`, etc.)

### 2. Context Ownership
- **`llvm/lib/IR/LLVMContextImpl.h`** — `LLVMContextImpl` holds all type uniquing tables: `DenseMap<unsigned, IntegerType*> IntegerTypes`, `FunctionTypeSet FunctionTypes`, `StructTypeSet AnonStructTypes`, `StringMap<StructType*> NamedStructTypes`, plus a `BumpPtrAllocator Alloc` for all type memory
- **`llvm/include/llvm/IR/LLVMContext.h`** / **`llvm/lib/IR/LLVMContext.cpp`** — Public API wrapping `LLVMContextImpl`

### 3. IR Type → Machine Type Lowering
- **`llvm/lib/CodeGen/ValueTypes.cpp`** — `EVT::getEVT(Type *Ty)` converts IR types to `EVT` (Extended Value Type)
- **`llvm/include/llvm/CodeGen/TargetLowering.h`** — `TargetLowering::getValueType()` wraps `EVT::getEVT` with pointer-size awareness
- **`llvm/lib/CodeGen/Analysis.cpp`** — `ComputeValueTypes()` and `ComputeValueVTs()` recursively decompose aggregate types (structs, arrays) into flat lists of EVTs
- **`llvm/lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/SelectionDAGBuilder.cpp`** — `visitLoad`, `visitStore`, and other visitors call `ComputeValueVT
... (truncated)

Also note that only one instance of a particular\\n39: /// type is ever created.  Thus seeing if two types are equal is a matter of\\n40: /// doing a trivial pointer comparison. To enforce that no two equal instances\\n41: /// are created, Type instances can only be created via static factory methods\\n42: /// in class Type and in derived classes. cast<FunctionType>(this)->getNumParams();\\n164: }\\n165: \\n166: /// A handy container for a FunctionType+Callee-pointer pair, which can be\\n167: /// passed around as a single entity. There are two different kinds of struct\\n199: /// types: Literal structs and Identified structs.\\n200: ///\\n201: /// Literal struct types (e.g. { i32, i32 }) are uniqued structurally, and must\\n202: /// always have a body when created.  You can get one of these by using one of\\n203: /// the StructType::get() forms.\\n204: ///\\n205: /// Identified structs (e.g. %foo or %42) may optionally have a name and are not\\n206: /// uniqued.  The names for identified structs are managed at the LLVMContext\\n207: /// level, so there can only be a single identified struct with a given name in\\n208: /// a particular LLVMContext.  Identified structs may also optionally be opaque\\n209: /// (have no body specified).  You get one of these by using one of the\\n210: /// StructType::create() forms.\\n211: ///\\n212: /// Independent of what kind of struct you have, the body of a struct type are\\n213: /// laid out in memory consecutively with the elements directly one after the\\n214: /// other (if the struct is packed) or (if not packed) with padding between the\\n215: /// elements as defined by DataLayout (which is required to match what the code\\n216: /// generator for a target expects).\\n217: ///\\n218: class StructType : public Type {\\n219:   StructType(LLVMContext &C) : Type(C, StructTyID) {}\\n220: delete;\\n244: \\n245:   /// This creates an identified struct.\\n246:   LLVM_ABI static StructType *create(LLVMContext &Context, StringRef Name);\\n247:   LLVM_ABI static StructType   LLVM_ABI static StructType *create(ArrayRef<Type *> Elements);\\n252:   LLVM_ABI static StructType *create(LLVMContext &Context,\\n253:                                      ArrayRef<Type *> 'n' is the\\n432:   /// minimum number of elements of type Ty contained within the vector, and\\n433:   /// 'vscale x' indicates that the total element count is an integer multiple\\n434:   /// of 'n', where the multiple is either guaranteed to be one, or is\\n435:   /// statically unknown at compile time.\\n436:   ///\\n437:   /// If the multiple is known to be 1, then the extra term is discarded in\\n438:   /// textual IR:\\n439:   ///\\n440:   /// <4 x i32>          - a vector containing 4 i32s\\n441:   /// <vscale x 4 x i32> - a vector containing an unknown integer multiple\\n442:   ///                      of 4 i32s\\n443: \\n444:   /// The element type of the vector.\\n445:   Type *ContainedType;\\n446: \\n447: protected:\\n448:   /// The element quantity of this vector. The meaning of this value depends\\n449:   /// on the type of vector:\\n450:   /// - For FixedVectorType = <ElementQuantity x ty>, there are\\n451:   ///   exactly ElementQuantity elements in this vector.\\n452:   /// - For ScalableVectorType = <vscale x ElementQuantity x ty>,\\n453:   ///   there are vscale * ElementQuantity elements in this vector, where\\n454:   ///   vscale is a runtime-constant integer greater than 0.\\n455:   const unsigned ElementQuantity;\\n456: \\n457:   LLVM_ABI VectorType(Type *ElType, unsigned EQ, Type::TypeID TID);\\n458: \\n459: public:\\n460:   VectorType(const VectorType &) = delete;\\n461:   VectorType &operator=(const VectorType &) = delete;\\n462: \\n463:   Type *getElementType() const { return ContainedType; }\\n464: \\n465:   /// This VectorType *getTruncatedElementVectorType(VectorType *VTy) {\\n501:     Type *EltTy;\\n502:     if (VTy->getElementType()->isFloatingPointTy()) {\\n503: Type Class Hierarchy (llvm/include/llvm/IR/Type.h, llvm/include/llvm/IR/DerivedTypes.h)\\n\\nThe root of the type system is the `Type` class defined in `llvm/include/llvm/IR/Type.h`. It is an immutable, uniqued class that holds a `TypeID` enum (e.g., `IntegerTyID`, `FunctionTyID`, `StructTyID`, `PointerTyID`, `ArrayTyID`, `FixedVectorTyID`, `ScalableVectorTyID`, `TargetExtTyID`, etc.) and a back-reference to the owning `LLVMContext`. Types are never freed once created.\\n\\nDerived types are declared in `llvm/include/llvm/IR/DerivedTypes.h` and implemented in `llvm/lib/IR/Type.cpp`:\\n- **`IntegerType`**: Represents arbitrary-width integers. Created via `IntegerType::get(LLVMContext &C, unsigned NumBits)`. Stores bit-width in the `SubclassData` field.\\n- **`FunctionType`**: Represents function signatures (return type + parameter types + vararg flag). Created via `FunctionType::get(Type *Result, ArrayRef<Type*> Params, bool isVarArg)`.\\n- **`StructType`**: Represents struct types. Literal structs (anonymous, uniqued structurally) are created via `StructType::get(LLVMContext &Context, ArrayRef<Type*> Elements, bool isPacked)`. Identified structs (named, not uniqued) are created via `StructType::create(LLVMContext &Context, StringRef Name)`.\\n- **`ArrayType`**, **`VectorType`** (`FixedVectorType`, `ScalableVectorType`), **`PointerType`**, **`TargetExtType`**: Other derived types.\\n\\n### 2. Context Ownership (llvm/lib/IR/LLVMContextImpl.h, llvm/lib/IR/LLVMContext.h, llvm/lib/IR/LLVMContext.cpp)\\n\\nAll type instances are owned by `LLVMContext` (via its opaque implementation `LLVMContextImpl` in `llvm/lib/IR/LLVMContextImpl.h`). The context holds:\\n- `DenseMap<unsigned, IntegerType *> IntegerTypes` \u2014 uniquing table for integer types by bit-width.\\n- `FunctionTypeSet FunctionTypes` \u2014 a `DenseSet<FunctionType *, FunctionTypeKeyInfo>` for uniquing function types by (return type, params, vararg).\\n- `StructTypeSet AnonStructTypes` \u2014 a `DenseSet<StructType *, AnonStructTypeKeyInfo>` for uniquing literal struct types.\\n- `StringMap<StructType *> NamedStructTypes` \u2014 for identified (named) struct types.\\n- `DenseMap<std::pair<Type *, uint64_t>, ArrayType *> ArrayTypes`, `DenseMap<std::pair<Type *, ElementCount>, VectorType *> VectorTypes`, `DenseMap<unsigned, PointerType *> PointerTypes`, `TargetExtTypeSet TargetExtTypes`.\\n- Pre-allocated singleton instances for primitive types: `Type VoidTy, LabelTy, HalfTy, BFloatTy, FloatTy, DoubleTy, ...` and `IntegerType Int1Ty, Int8Ty, Int16Ty, Int32Ty, Int64Ty, Int128Ty`.\\n- A `BumpPtrAllocator Alloc` used to allocate all type objects.\\n\\nThe `LLVMContextImpl` also defines the key-info structs (`AnonStructTypeKeyInfo`, `FunctionTypeKeyInfo`, `TargetExtTypeKeyInfo`) used for hashing and equality in the uniquing sets.\\n\\nType factory methods (e.g., `IntegerType::get`, `FunctionType::get`, `StructType::get`) look up or insert into these tables via `C.pImpl->IntegerTypes`, `C.pImpl->FunctionTypes`, etc., ensuring that only one instance of each structurally equivalent type exists per context.\\n\\n### 3. IR Type to Machine Type Lowering in SelectionDAG\\n\\nThe lowering chain from LLVM IR types to SelectionDAG machine types proceeds through several layers:\\n\\n**Step 1: `EVT::getEVT(Type *Ty)` \u2014 `llvm/lib/CodeGen/ValueTypes.cpp`**\\nThis function converts an LLVM IR `Type *` to an `EVT` (Extended Value Type, defined in `llvm/include/llvm/CodeGen/ValueTypes.h`). It switches on `Ty->getTypeID()`: integers become `getIntegerVT(...)`, vectors become `getVectorVT(...)`, and other types fall through to `MVT::getVT(Ty, HandleUnknown)`.\\n\\n**Step 2: `TargetLowering::getValueType(const DataLayout &DL, Type *Ty)` \u2014 `llvm/include/llvm/CodeGen/TargetLowering.h`**\\nThis method wraps `EVT::getEVT` with pointer-type awareness: pointer types are lowered to the target's native pointer EVT via `getPointerTy(DL, AddrSpace)`, and vector-of-pointer types are handled similarly. This is the primary API used by code generation passes to convert IR types to machine types.\\n\\n**Step 3: `ComputeValueTypes` and `ComputeValueVTs` \u2014 `llvm/lib/CodeGen/Analysis.cpp` (declared in `llvm/include/llvm/CodeGen/Analysis.h`)**\\n`ComputeValueTypes` recursively decomposes aggregate IR types (structs, arrays) into a flat list of scalar `Type *` values. `ComputeValueVTs` then calls `TLI.getValueType(DL, Ty)` on each scalar type to produce a flat list of `EVT`s. This is the bridge that handles struct and array decomposition for code generation.\\n\\n**Step 4: `SelectionDAGBuilder` \u2014 `llvm/lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/SelectionDAGBuilder.cpp`**\\nThe `SelectionDAGBuilder` translates LLVM IR instructions into SelectionDAG nodes. For example:\\n- `visitLoad(const LoadInst &I)` calls `ComputeValueVTs(TLI, DAG.getDataLayout(), Ty, ValueVTs, &MemVTs, &Offsets)` to get the EVTs for the loaded type, then creates `ISD::LOAD` nodes for each component.\\n- `visitStore(const StoreInst &I)` similarly decomposes the stored type.\\n- Many other visitors call `TLI.getValueType(DAG.getDataLayout(), I.getType())` directly for scalar types.\\n- Function argument lowering (in `lowerFormalArguments`) calls `ComputeValueTypes` and then `TLI->getValueType(DL, ArgTy)` for each argument type.\\n\\n**Step 5: `SelectionDAGISel` \u2014 `llvm/lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/SelectionDAGISel.cpp`**\\nThe instruction selector operates on the SelectionDAG nodes (which carry EVT/MVT type information) and selects target machine instructions.\\n\\n### Summary of the Chain\\n\\n```\\nType creation API (IntegerType::get, FunctionType::get, StructType::get, etc.)\\n  [llvm/include/llvm/IR/DerivedTypes.h, llvm/lib/IR/Type.cpp]\\n  \u2193\\nContext ownership & uniquing (LLVMContextImpl: IntegerTypes, FunctionTypes, AnonStructTypes, NamedStructTypes)\\n  [llvm/lib/IR/LLVMContextImpl.h, llvm/lib/IR/LLVMContext.cpp]\\n  \u2193\\nEVT::getEVT(Type *Ty)  \u2014 IR type \u2192 Extended Value Type\\n  [llvm/lib/CodeGen/ValueTypes.cpp, llvm/include/llvm/CodeGen/ValueTypes.h]\\n  \u2193\\nTargetLowering::getValueType(DataLayout, Type *)  \u2014 pointer-aware IR\u2192EVT\\n  [llvm/include/llvm/CodeGen/TargetLowering.h]\\n  \u2193\\nComputeValueTypes / ComputeValueVTs  \u2014 aggregate decomposition\\n  [llvm/lib/CodeGen/Analysis.cpp, llvm/include/llvm/CodeGen/Analysis.h]\\n  \u2193\\nSelectionDAGBuilder::visitLoad/visitStore/etc.  \u2014 IR instructions \u2192 DAG nodes with EVT\\n  [llvm/lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/SelectionDAGBuilder.cpp]\\n  \u2193\\nSelectionDAGISel  \u2014 DAG nodes \u2192 machine instructions\\n  [llvm/lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/SelectionDAGISel.cpp]\\n```\"\n}\n",
